<div id="review_1718549166" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1718549166" />
    <a title="Stevie Kincade" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/56187822-stevie-kincade"><img alt="Stevie Kincade" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1476505168p2/56187822.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1718549166?book_show_action=true">Feb 01, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stevie Kincade" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stevie Kincade" href="/user/show/56187822-stevie-kincade">Stevie Kincade</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56187822-stevie-kincade?shelf=published-2015">published-2015</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56187822-stevie-kincade?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56187822-stevie-kincade?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/56187822-stevie-kincade?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1718549166" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13549495669561174791">(Audiobook – 4.5 stars) The Traitor Baru Cormorant is unlike any book I have ever read before.<br/><br/>I have read plenty of tales of revenge, empire building, totalitarianism, deceit and subterfuge. I have read fantasies that contain no magic or dragons. I have never read a book with all these elements where our main character is an <i>accountant</i> who’s main weapons are guile, inflation, market manipulation and management of logistics.<br/><br/><i>Wait! Don’t stop reading!</i> I know the idea of a controlled sub-prime mortg</span>
  <span id="freeText13549495669561174791" style="display:none">(Audiobook – 4.5 stars) The Traitor Baru Cormorant is unlike any book I have ever read before.<br /><br />I have read plenty of tales of revenge, empire building, totalitarianism, deceit and subterfuge. I have read fantasies that contain no magic or dragons. I have never read a book with all these elements where our main character is an <i>accountant</i> who’s main weapons are guile, inflation, market manipulation and management of logistics.<br /><br /><i>Wait! Don’t stop reading!</i> I know the idea of a controlled sub-prime mortgage crises in Fantasyland doesn’t exactly <i>sound</i> riveting but I’ll be damned if this book didn’t pull me from the edge of my seat and drag me through the emotional wringer. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1405832842?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Brad</a> has noted his love of this growing “Economi-punk” genre but it is completely new to me. Consider me intrigued. I would love to read more of this genre as well as anything further from Seth Dickinson.<br /><br />In “Traitor” the “Evil Empire” is the all controlling “Masquerade” who come across as villainous Nazi stand-ins. Instead of overt mass murder and massacre, the Masquerade use the weapons of indoctrination, starvation, disease and laws on breeding and “hygiene” (sex) to control the conquered populace. The Masquerade are not an enemy that will be defeated by military might, a much more subtle game of thrones will be required. <br /><br />I found the first third of the book gripping, the middle third confusing and not particularly enjoyable - and the last third utterly astounding (and not particularly enjoyable). One of the things I learned on Goodreads (I believe paraphrasing Gene Wolfe) is that a reader finds a book satisfying when it raises a certain set of expectations - then fulfils those expectations in a way the reader could not predict, but in hindsight seemed inevitable. Holy crap did this book do that to me. I thought I knew what was going to happen and then I got slapped across the face with a giant salmon and walked around in a daze for a few hours afterwards. <br /><br />This book does have a glaring flaw that keeps it from a 5 star rating from me. It is not its constant use of the word “palimpsest”, although if you took a shot of your favourite adult beverage every time you heard “palimpsest” you would be one drunk monkey. <br /><br />In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1552202798?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">Erik’s</a> brilliant review of this book where he breaks down the cardinal sins of reviewing (very guilty party here) he gives us the memorable line <i> if description were money, Seth Dickinson would make our old friend Ebenezer Scrooge look like Andrew Carnegie.</i> He is completely correct. I have read enough Robert Jordan to be quite happy to read a book with nary a description of a township or the rolling hills of the countryside or the craftsmanship of a tea-set. <br /><br /><i>However</i> in the middle 3rd of the book when the plot revolves around a host of Dukes and Duchesses with weird names and we are given barely a sentence that tells us anything about them, I found the machinations almost impossible to follow. Dickinson might as well have called the characters “Dukes A, B, C and D” because I could tell you absolutely nothing about them. I couldn’t remember their names let alone anything about them…other than that they were Dukes and Duchesses of a certain province. So when A and B move against C - and D was reluctant to join forces and so forth it meant almost nothing to me. This was a pretty big flaw because I love my “palace intrigue” books and this was a substantial portion of the plot.<br /><br />The book isn’t all politics and inflation effects. I actually thought that once we moved onto the “big battle” sequences the tactics and strategy described were outstanding and much more interesting to me than the typical descriptions of daring and bloody glory on the battlefield. You will just have to suspend disbelief that our financial wizard is also something of a master military strategist. <br /><br />I really enjoyed Christine Marshall’s narration of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1718524245" rel="nofollow noopener">Infomocracy</a> so it was easy to purchase this book knowing I was already on board with the narrator. She goes with a “less is more” narration that kept me focused on the story and not the voice actor.<br /><br />So there are obvious flaws with “Traitor” but this book packed a massive emotional wallop that pretty much floored me. It also managed to cover familiar themes in new and interesting ways that lifted “Traitor” overall, far, far above the average fantasy fare.</span>
  <a data-text-id="13549495669561174791" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText7560509497501738600" style="display:none">Probably one of the best book I have ever read. My favorite book so far of the year. <br /><br />This book is so different from any type of fantasy that I have ever read. Its like nothing out there, its so unique. Good job on a well done debut that will divide people/readers as much as Thomas Convent or The Magicians. Its like if all the Grimdark authors started to add something different to all there works, but still is realistic and considered to be Grimdark. <br /><br />Basically in my opinion, this book is Grimdark compared to all the authors currently writing Grimdark. They are writing cliche Tolkien instead of Grimdark compared to this book. That's how good the book is and unique that will beat and punch the crap out of the read and turn the viewpoint of the genre on its head. <div id="review_2546383124" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2546383124" />
    <a title="Claudia ✨" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39374372-claudia"><img alt="Claudia ✨" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602014152p2/39374372.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2546383124?book_show_action=true">Jul 26, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Claudia ✨" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Claudia ✨" href="/user/show/39374372-claudia">Claudia ✨</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39374372-claudia?shelf=feminist-reads">feminist-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39374372-claudia?shelf=year-2019">year-2019</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/39374372-claudia?shelf=lgbtqia">lgbtqia</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2546383124" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3957460366183858915"><i>“This is the truth. You will know because it hurts.”</i><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23444482.The_Traitor_Baru_Cormorant__The_Masquerade___1_' title='The Traitor Baru Cormorant (The Masquerade, #1) by Seth Dickinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Traitor Baru Cormorant</a> is one of a kind. It's a book that will lie to you, gladly, luring you into a sense of false safety. Then it will pull the carpet from underneath your feet laughing and you fall to your ass like the gullible fool you are, completely astonished.<br/><br/>It's taken me a few weeks to collect myself after that fall, to try to settle in that truth that <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5760737.Seth_Dickinson' title='Seth Dickinson' rel='nofollow noopener'>Seth Dickinson</a> first kept from us and then so smugly shoved us in. <b>His book is r</b></span>
  <span id="freeText3957460366183858915" style="display:none"><i>“This is the truth. You will know because it hurts.”</i><br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23444482.The_Traitor_Baru_Cormorant__The_Masquerade___1_" title="The Traitor Baru Cormorant (The Masquerade, #1) by Seth Dickinson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Traitor Baru Cormorant</a> is one of a kind. It's a book that will lie to you, gladly, luring you into a sense of false safety. Then it will pull the carpet from underneath your feet laughing and you fall to your ass like the gullible fool you are, completely astonished.<br /><br />It's taken me a few weeks to collect myself after that fall, to try to settle in that truth that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5760737.Seth_Dickinson" title="Seth Dickinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Seth Dickinson</a> first kept from us and then so smugly shoved us in. <b>His book is raw, ugly and fantastic.</b><br /><br />Baru Cormorant is an island girl, living happily with her two fathers and mother on Taranoke. Her family is big, she knows all of the stars and the food is plentiful. And then, sails appear on the horizon. Sails that bring new, <i>appropriate</i> customs and ways to live, that bring an Empire of Masks and conquerers. <br /><br />But Baru is a brilliant, and the Empire wants brilliant minds among them. They take her into their school, mold her and teach her what is right and what is wrong while doing the same to Taranoke outside, without caring for its people. But Baru cares. She knows that there is nothing she can do to threaten that huge Empire though - except for destroying it from the inside. So that is what she will do. Climb, not caring who she tramples underneath her feet, and then save her people. Whatever the cost. <br /><br /><i>“Without any outward sign or motion, in the wreckage of herself, she donned her armor, made it firm around her heart. Raise her mask: a cold discipline, a steel beneath her skin. <br />Grow comfortable, she told herself. It will never come off.”</i><br /><br />Simply put, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23444482.The_Traitor_Baru_Cormorant__The_Masquerade___1_" title="The Traitor Baru Cormorant (The Masquerade, #1) by Seth Dickinson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Traitor Baru Cormorant</a> is about colonalization. It's about what happens when those well-meaning and "civilized" strangers shows up at your doorstep, entering your home and then claiming it as theirs. It's also about what happens to those that rebel against these strangers, and what it takes to survive it.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5760737.Seth_Dickinson" title="Seth Dickinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Dickinson</a> writing was often beautiful and poetic, but never shied away from the ugliness of this theme. Baru as a character encompassed this. She was bold and manipulative, too clever and cynical. Scarred by what had been done to herself, her family and her home. <br /><br />I was drawn in from the first chapter, the only one that we got to spend in Taranoke. After that it did go a bit slow - this isn't a fast-paced book by any means, as it's mostly political business and backstabbing going on. But even if I wasn't hooked, I was still very intrigued and needed to see how everything would go. <br /><br />The last chapters though - jesus christ, I was <i>glued</i> to this book. I was gaping, not believing what I was reading. I rate this book a four star since I didn't find myself completely in love with it, which is probably half due to how hyped it was, <b>but that ending and the experience it gave me is, without a single doubt, worth five stars.</b><br /><br />I would like to give <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5760737.Seth_Dickinson" title="Seth Dickinson" rel="nofollow noopener">Seth Dickinson</a> a round of applause. It takes brains, talent and guts to write a book like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/23444482.The_Traitor_Baru_Cormorant__The_Masquerade___1_" title="The Traitor Baru Cormorant (The Masquerade, #1) by Seth Dickinson" rel="nofollow noopener">The Traitor Baru Cormorant</a>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3957460366183858915" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1656095560" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1656095560" />
    <a title="gio" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/23204207-gio"><img alt="gio" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597613414p2/23204207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1656095560?book_show_action=true">Jun 02, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="gio" class="user" itemprop="url" name="gio" href="/user/show/23204207-gio">gio</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1656095560" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12259052413503616764">The Traitor Baru Cormorant caught my eye here on goodreads, while I was mindlessly looking for interesting titles. It had few ratings, but the plot sounded quite cool and TOR rarely publishes trash when it comes to fantasy. The ebook was cheap so...I was sold.<br/><br/>Can't say I'm disappointed. Actually I was extremely surprised, and in a positive way, by pretty much everything in this book. It's a political fantasy, it's clever, cunning, twisted, cruel. Which in my book makes it pretty much perfect. <br/><br/>Ob</span>
  <span id="freeText12259052413503616764" style="display:none">The Traitor Baru Cormorant caught my eye here on goodreads, while I was mindlessly looking for interesting titles. It had few ratings, but the plot sounded quite cool and TOR rarely publishes trash when it comes to fantasy. The ebook was cheap so...I was sold.<br /><br />Can't say I'm disappointed. Actually I was extremely surprised, and in a positive way, by pretty much everything in this book. It's a political fantasy, it's clever, cunning, twisted, cruel. Which in my book makes it pretty much perfect. <br /><br />Obviously Baru is the main character. She's a quiet, curious child, with a lively, bright mind, living in a small island with her mother and her fathers (yep, plural). Then one day she sees the Masquerade's ships looming on the horizon. In a few years her land in conquered, by the Empire's money, knowledge and political games and Baru sees her beloved island's customs criminalized and her culture erased. <br />But Baru is patient. She enters the Empire's new school, learns their rules, plays their games, tries to discover their secrets. She has one task ahead of her: become part of their system and destroy it from the inside, no matter what it takes.<br /><br />The plot might not seem extremely original, but:<br />1) the execution of the idea is spectacular<br />2) you actually rarely see fantasy like this. I love political fantasy (think The Winner's Kiss when it comes to ya) but I feel like they're often underrated. People usually prefer fantasy with magic (and I love that too) or war, or both, but politcal fantasy can be stunning too, in a more subtle way. <br /><br />The Traitor Baru Cormorant is a subtle book, and that's why I loved it. It's subtle, but stunning. Cunning, sly, quite cruel. There's no space for feelings in Baru's life. She does what she believes it's necessary to overthrow the Empire, no matter if it costs her her humanity. She needs to be ruthless if she wants to succeed. That doesn't mean that she isn't human, because she has her weaknesses too, but she's extremely complex and twisted. She's not what I'd call a good person, and that makes it even more fascinating.<br /><br />If you like morally gray books, with twisted and sly characters, then this is your book. </span>
  <a data-text-id="12259052413503616764" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('c9OUGpIKX/ejmoYVCagudcM15GbAE0UMrXeJtXmNaiiZskIfDsv+IjjULi7hFiogwRKvTAXXzXbIAAPBWZ6hUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('Urre/Az6yuQYxM/bSpLWhyOghEAWTL+Fs0HuFn2Xv5K42wj5kDtrMYOKZ+CiLNLSIYfPatOIN//WNmRiXYR06A==')})
  }

  <span id="freeText18444187308358047293" style="display:none">Since his 2012 debut, Seth's fiction has appeared in Clarkesworld, Lightspeed, Analog, and nearly every other major science fiction and fantasy market. <br /><br />He's a lapsed student of social neuroscience, where he studied the role of racial bias in police shootings, and the writer of much of the lore and fictional flavor for Bungie Studios' smash hit Destiny. In his spare time he works on the collaborative space opera Blue Planet: War in Heaven.<br /><br />THE TRAITOR BARU CORMORANT is his first novel.</span>
